  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18189974049799445931">What dangers do runaway demigods Luke and Thalia face on their way to Camp Half-Blood? Are Percy and Annabeth up to the task of rescuing stolen goods from a fire-breathing giant who doesn't take kindly to intruders?   <span id="freeText18189974049799445931" style="display:none">What dangers do runaway demigods Luke and Thalia face on their way to Camp Half-Blood? Are Percy and Annabeth up to the task of rescuing stolen goods from a fire-breathing giant who doesn't take kindly to intruders? How exactly are Leo, Piper, and Jason supposed to find a runaway table, dodge a band of party-loving Maenads (who just might be a little psychotic), and stave off a massive explosion...all in one hour or less? With his trademark wit and creativity, Rick Riordan answers these questions and more in three never-before-seen short stories that provide vital back-story to the Heroes of Olympus and Percy Jackson books. Original art, enlightening character interviews and profiles, puzzles, and a quiz add to the fun in this action-packed collection.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/106337588-caroline">Caroline</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There are three short stories inside it. One of which is Luke Castellan's diary, about the time he and Thalia Grace met Annabeth, and their adventures<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There are three short stories inside it. One of which is Luke Castellan's diary, about the time he and Thalia Grace met Annabeth, and their adventures before it. It explains how Thalia gets her shield, Aegis. The second story is about how Percy and Annabeth must find Hermes' staff that was stolen by a fire-breathing giant. The third story is written by Rick Riordan's son Haley. It is about a mortal author who gets involved in the demigod world, because of a child of Hecate who wants his help.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer367176518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11088496015511009270">I got this for my birthday, which was awesome. I sat down on the couch and didn't talk to anybody for several hours.<br/>It was great to see Luke and Thalia before they reached Camp Halfblood or any of the later craziness occured. I think I like Luke now more than I ever did.<br/>The Percy & Annabeth Story: Oh, how I've missed them. Together. In the same book/shortstory/whatever. I like first person perspective better than third person in general, and I love Percy's narration. Plus George and Martha went </span>
  <span id="freeText11088496015511009270" style="display:none">I got this for my birthday, which was awesome. I sat down on the couch and didn't talk to anybody for several hours.<br />It was great to see Luke and Thalia before they reached Camp Halfblood or any of the later craziness occured. I think I like Luke now more than I ever did.<br />The Percy &amp; Annabeth Story: Oh, how I've missed them. Together. In the same book/shortstory/whatever. I like first person perspective better than third person in general, and I love Percy's narration. Plus George and Martha went Lazer Mode. I've been waiting for this since the Last Olympian.<br />It was also great to see Leo, Piper, and Jason (but especially Leo) again. We've only really known them for one book, and I spent the whole time reading it thinking, WHERE IS PERCY JACKSON! HE IS MISSING! FIND HIM!. Still, it was nice to see them again, and the Maenads were pretty cool. Utterly terrifying, yes, but cool.<br />Finally, I come to Son of Magic. It was a little darker than some of his dad's stories, which I'm totally cool with. I &lt;3 the dark stuff. There were times when I started thinking, Percy Jackson, how dare you. Then I caught myself. Still, I loved Alabaster, and I hope he shows up in a Heroes of Olympus book, even for just a brief fight to the death.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14941707051547378629">You know I love anything by Rick Riordan! :D<br/><br/><b> The Diary of Luke Castellan: </b><br/><br/>Thank you, Rick, for writing this story!! It was interesting to know about the dangers Luke and Thalia faced before The Lightning Thief and before Annabeth. And now I know how Aegis came to be and how exactly Annabeth got that dagger! :P<br/><br/><b> Percy Jackson and the Staff of Hermes: </b><br/><br/>Nice great story about Percabeth! :P I noticed how he put a reference to what happened in the past books he wrote.   <span id="freeText14941707051547378629" style="display:none">You know I love anything by Rick Riordan! :D<br /><br /><b> The Diary of Luke Castellan: </b><br /><br />Thank you, Rick, for writing this story!! It was interesting to know about the dangers Luke and Thalia faced before The Lightning Thief and before Annabeth. And now I know how Aegis came to be and how exactly Annabeth got that dagger! :P<br /><br /><b> Percy Jackson and the Staff of Hermes: </b><br /><br />Nice great story about Percabeth! :P I noticed how he put a reference to what happened in the past books he wrote. I love the humor Rick always puts in his books. <br /><br /><blockquote> "But fighting with her? That came naturally. Hmm...that sounded wrong. Oh well." </blockquote><br /><br />XD. That's all I have to say on that subject.<br /><br /><b> Leo Valdez and the Quest for Buford: </b><br /><br />Funny weird-ish story about Jason, Piper, and Leo has with Leo's table, Buford *snicker* and the Maenads.Or however you spell it. <br /><br /><b> Son of Magic: </b><br /><br />HALEY RIORDAN, BLESS YOUR HEART.<br /><br />This story was absolutely amazing! :D I love how he answered the questions about the Mist and how monsters are able to track demigods. And it was nice to actually hear a story about one of the demigods that fought for Kronos. And it included a mortal! :o<br /></span>

<div id="review_410538443" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410538443" />
    <a title="Natasha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7991963-natasha"><img alt="Natasha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516531224p2/7991963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410538443?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha" href="/user/show/7991963-natasha">Natasha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7991963-natasha?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7991963-natasha?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410538443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6910088944168809771"><i>The Demigod Diaries</i>, like <i>The Demigod Files</i>, serves as an interlude between two of Rick Riordan's books in the main series. While all the stories in the <i>Files</i> all happen during the summer between <i>The Battle of the Labyrinth</i> and <i>The Last Olympian</i>, the four stories in this book all happen at different times, which I found helped me understand and become more involved in the Percy Jackson universe.<br/><br/>The Diary of Luke Castellan was a really interesting read for me. It's interesting to see Luke as the </span>
  <span id="freeText6910088944168809771" style="display:none"><i>The Demigod Diaries</i>, like <i>The Demigod Files</i>, serves as an interlude between two of Rick Riordan's books in the main series. While all the stories in the <i>Files</i> all happen during the summer between <i>The Battle of the Labyrinth</i> and <i>The Last Olympian</i>, the four stories in this book all happen at different times, which I found helped me understand and become more involved in the Percy Jackson universe.<br /><br />The Diary of Luke Castellan was a really interesting read for me. It's interesting to see Luke as the 'good guy' he was back in <i>The Lightning Thief</i>, and to see why exactly Thalia and Annabeth admired him so much. The Thalia and Luke dynamic was really cute too; I'll admit my heart cried when Luke talked about how he could never refuse Thalia. I also extremely liked how it also told the story of Annabeth's knife and how Luke found it and that was extremely touching. At times, however, I forgot that it was Luke narrating and not Percy, because their narration styles were eerily similar. But I think that's just a Rick Riordan thing.<br /><br />Percy Jackson and the Staff of Hermes was everything I have waited for since I finished <i>The Last Olympian</i>. We have Percy and Annabeth on a date, kicking butt and just generally being cute. It's sweet how even though they're dating, there are still some things so Percy and Annabeth that they haven't changed. And Percy's concerns about Annabeth being hurt are generally just really sweet and I really missed First Person Percy POV. It's nice to see Percy in a new light and see him through other people's eyes, but I missed the snark that goes in Percy's head. Bless him.<br /><br />Leo Valdez and the Quest for Buford basically had me in stitches. While the first story gave me more understanding and the second warm fuzzies, Leo's story just made me crack up in laughter. The fact he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[tried to pretend to be Dionysus <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> made me almost fall off my chair. There are some things that only Leo Valdez can pull off -- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[like managing to create a party area in Bunker Nine within a minute. Definitely badass, Valdez! --  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> while Jason and Piper, whom he's pulled into his problems are kind of confused by the whole thing while trying to help him out.<br /><br />And finally, we get to Son of Magic, by Rick's son, Haley. For someone my age, the story was pretty much amazing. I can't say that I can write like that. Alabaster's story is quite strange and I grew to like but extremely dislike the characters. Dr Claymore was kind of an idiotic mortal and Alabaster hated Percy Jackson because he destroyed Kronos's army and expected the minor gods to yield because of a wish. At times, I felt mad at Percy instead of Alabaster -- and even realising Claymore acts like an idiotic mortal because he is one. However, it kind of really creeped me out because it was very deep and dark, a darkness his father's stories never reach because they always have that witty humour strung through the whole thing. Still, it was a great read.<br /><br />I read through this book in a couple of hours, and I just need me some <i>Mark of Athena</i>! Thank goodness the countdown's less than a month and I can't wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6910088944168809771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I also liked that his son also had a story at the end of the book. This is a good book to read for any fans o</span>

What I loved most was reading about how the Author began writing the Percy Jackson series - he was inspired by his son who was diagnosed with ADHD and dyslexia (as are the demigods) and that Percy Jackson sprang to life in bedtime stories he told his son. I also liked that his son also had a story at the end of the book. This is a good book to read for any fans of the Percy Jackson series.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/448656792?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer448656792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14237218534758664497">Loved it! I loved that we got to see Annabeth and Percy's romance <i>before</i> he disappears. I also loved that we got to see another side of the deceased Son of Hermes, Luke when he was younger and how he along with Thalia acted as surrogate parents to a then 7 year-old Annabeth.<br/><br/>Another great aspect of this book is the interview with George and Martha, the snakes that reside on Hermes' staff.<br/><br/>This book also contains the debut short story, Son of Magic by Rick's son Harley, the inspiration for the Perc</span>
  <span id="freeText14237218534758664497" style="display:none">Loved it! I loved that we got to see Annabeth and Percy's romance <i>before</i> he disappears. I also loved that we got to see another side of the deceased Son of Hermes, Luke when he was younger and how he along with Thalia acted as surrogate parents to a then 7 year-old Annabeth.<br /><br />Another great aspect of this book is the interview with George and Martha, the snakes that reside on Hermes' staff.<br /><br />This book also contains the debut short story, Son of Magic by Rick's son Harley, the inspiration for the Percy Jackson series who was only 16 when he wrote the story.<br /><br />Like always, Rick combines fun and mythology and rolls out a book that can brighten your day if you're having a rotten one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14237218534758664497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/15725893-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141344379" href="/book/show/15925005-the-demigod-diaries">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15725893-anna?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1110426652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13563626701562703074">This was a nice addition to the <i>Heroes of Olympus</i> series, though not a completely necessary one in Uncle Rick's case (I'll explain what I mean).<br/><br/>The book includes a few short stories centered around Luke, Percy and Leo. In Luke's story we take a peek in his life before he came to Camp Half-Blood and his relationship with Thalia and how they came to meet Annabeth. It was a nice addition in the sense that we get to see what Luke has been through and the fact that he didn't 'become a bad person' out</span>
  <span id="freeText13563626701562703074" style="display:none">This was a nice addition to the <i>Heroes of Olympus</i> series, though not a completely necessary one in Uncle Rick's case (I'll explain what I mean).<br /><br />The book includes a few short stories centered around Luke, Percy and Leo. In Luke's story we take a peek in his life before he came to Camp Half-Blood and his relationship with Thalia and how they came to meet Annabeth. It was a nice addition in the sense that we get to see what Luke has been through and the fact that he didn't 'become a bad person' out of the blackness of his heart.<br /><br />Percy's and Leo's stories, I believe were just added in case you missed those favourite characters and would have kisy liked a little story in their point of view. Nothing terribly exciting happens, just a normal day in a demigod's life.<br /><br />However, what I enjoyed the most was the last story, <i>The Son of Magic</i>, which is written by Rick's son. I loved his foreword on how Percy came to be and the fact that his son is basically responsible for your favourite demigod and I felt very proud after reading the story, because it is really good and it definitely adds to the whole demigod world.<br />It gives you certain answers, and very good answers, to some questions about the demigods and Rick himself tells you that he wishes he came up with this facts in the first place.<br /><i>The Son of Magic</i> is definitely the highlight of this bundle.<br /><br />If you feel like you miss the gang, then you can pick this up, but all the more pick it for Haley's story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13563626701562703074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14396296127205335862" style="display:none">It's amazing to see the person who was the inspiration behind Percy Jackson contributing a story to Percy's world.I really wanted to know what happened to the demigods on Kronos's side.Were they condemned to the Filelds of Punishment ?Were they rejected by Camp Half Blood and left to fend for themselves?This story finally removed those doubts.And it's also interesting to know how monsters sniff out demigods.Also,I got to learn something-monsters aren't always bad in the first place-sometimes they are embittered and turned into monsters by the gods(especially that insufferable goddess ,Hera).Lamia and Medusa ,for instance.I rather like Haley Riordan's serious tone in the story.It's quite a a change from Rick's light hearted way of handling even the most dangerous situations in PJO.Hope Riordan Jr. contributes some more stories to the PJO universe.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301752937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3223285612509957107">Obviously, only for hardcore fans of Riordan's Greek and Roman demigods. I liked it more than the similar <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3992598.The_Demigod_Files__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians_' title='The Demigod Files (Percy Jackson and the Olympians) by Rick Riordan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Demigod Files</a>, though there's nothing here that made me quite as happy as Bob the Titan had. There are four stories here, each told from a different perspective. First, one of Luke and Thalia's adventures from their days on the run, before they met Annabeth. Luke's voice is distinct enough from Percy's, in no small part because of how bitter he already was. Next, Percy and Annabeth attem</span>
  <span id="freeText3223285612509957107" style="display:none">Obviously, only for hardcore fans of Riordan's Greek and Roman demigods. I liked it more than the similar <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3992598.The_Demigod_Files__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians_" title="The Demigod Files (Percy Jackson and the Olympians) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Demigod Files</a>, though there's nothing here that made me quite as happy as Bob the Titan had. There are four stories here, each told from a different perspective. First, one of Luke and Thalia's adventures from their days on the run, before they met Annabeth. Luke's voice is distinct enough from Percy's, in no small part because of how bitter he already was. Next, Percy and Annabeth attempt to have a date, which obviously cannot be allowed to stand. This one is set shortly after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4502507.The_Last_Olympian__Percy_Jackson_and_the_Olympians___5_" title="The Last Olympian (Percy Jackson and the Olympians, #5) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Olympian</a>. The third story is a Leo, Piper, and Jason adventure, with Leo as the lead character. You'll need to have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7624272.The_Lost_Hero__Heroes_of_Olympus___1_" title="The Lost Hero (Heroes of Olympus, #1) by Rick Riordan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Hero</a> for that one. All three are fun adventures, that fit into the overall world Riordan created without being something that you'd need to seek out. <br /><br />The last story in the book was actually written by Riordan's sixteen year old son, Haley. And honestly, I was impressed. His focus is one of the demigods who sided with Kronos, and it answers questions about what happened to them, the Mist, and the nature of monsters. Cool stuff, for a fan. And Haley is a good enough writer to make it a fun read, too. <br /><br />So, for a Percy Jackson fan, is it worth it? Absolutely. But if you're a Percy Jackson fan, you already knew that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3223285612509957107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13297071241707676513">I love Percy's relationship with Hermes.   <span id="freeText13297071241707676513" style="display:none">I love Percy's relationship with Hermes. The way they converse is so casual and friend-like (Percy did refer to him as a "personal friend), Percy was comfortable with teasing Hermes and being sarcastic with him, but defended him to the giant ("Hermes is a way better salesman than you"). The way Hermes "looked like he was about to cry" was quite cute and surprising for a god. Nonetheless he chose Percy (instead of his children) to recover his most important possession. He trusted Percy to succeed and keep it a secret, even though the staff is literally his god hood and that loosing it would make him a laughing stock. Percy's interaction with Martha and George also shows that he sees them as friends instead of just an item. The snakes were ultra-cute, sleeping with their "bulging bellies" and having Hemes patting their heads. Also Hermes thanked them for the favour!! I mean did ANY other gods thanked heroes for anything? Nope. Proving that Hermes is the best god ever. And... he gave them a dinner date in Paris!!! He dressed them up and snapped them to Paris!! Holy Hermes! </span>

Loved them!<br/><br/>If there was one short story I was looking forward to the most in this book, it was the last one called Son of Magic. But this story was actually written by Rick Riordan's son, Haley Riordan.   <span id="freeText1000322075206230776" style="display:none">More companion short stories in the Camp Half-Blood universe. Loved them!<br /><br />If there was one short story I was looking forward to the most in this book, it was the last one called Son of Magic. But this story was actually written by Rick Riordan's son, Haley Riordan. And may I just say this right now:<br /><br /><b> HALEY DID EXCELLENT! </b><br /><br />I know the whole background story of Rick's son and how it was him who inspired Percy Jackson in the first place. From having trouble reading as a little kid to now reading books and now writing this short story, I am so proud of this kid. What Haley wrote, not only is it about a son of Hecate, but what he created reveals some deep secrets of why there is a Mist that sets that barrier between half-bloods and humans and how monsters track people so easily with the use of technology. Something we've been dying to know.<br /><br /><i> Like father, like son </i><br /><br />Rick and Haley have come full circle in writing. I hope that one day, Haley Riordan will be the next bestselling author.<br /><br />Let's get this part out of the way: Rick's three short stories were fantastic too. As usual, rapidly thrilling and humorous.<br /><br />My favorite of the three was The Diary of Luke Castellan. It's obvious, it's Luke's diary. Without spoilers given, reading Luke's story from a long time ago before Percy Jackson had completely changed my view of Luke entirely than I first thought of him in Percy Jackson and the Olympians series. It was the system in the way of good guys gone bad. Yet, you have to end up expressing sympathy for this kid knowing what he used to be.</span>

<div id="review_404402459" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404402459" />
    <a title="Shawne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/284285-shawne"><img alt="Shawne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187283272p2/284285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/404402459?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawne" href="/user/show/284285-shawne">Shawne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Percy Jackson fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/284285-shawne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404402459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3561549549176851927">I'm on a bit of a Rick Riordan kick right now, evidently - and I was so glad to have this recently-released short-story collection (set in the <i>Percy Jackson</i> universe) to read after ripping through <i>The Serpent's Shadow</i>. It's been a while since I've read <i>The Demigod Files</i>, but from what I recall, I do feel that this anthology boasts a quartet of stronger, more memorable stories that very competently do their job in whetting our appetites for the forthcoming <i>Mark Of Athena</i>.<br/><br/>Three of the four stories</span>
  <span id="freeText3561549549176851927" style="display:none">I'm on a bit of a Rick Riordan kick right now, evidently - and I was so glad to have this recently-released short-story collection (set in the <i>Percy Jackson</i> universe) to read after ripping through <i>The Serpent's Shadow</i>. It's been a while since I've read <i>The Demigod Files</i>, but from what I recall, I do feel that this anthology boasts a quartet of stronger, more memorable stories that very competently do their job in whetting our appetites for the forthcoming <i>Mark Of Athena</i>.<br /><br />Three of the four stories in this volume are written by Riordan, and whether or not intentionally, they very nicely cover both a lot of history and emotional ground in his Olympian universe. <i>The Diary Of Luke Castellan</i> harks back to adventures that took place even before the first <i>Percy Jackson</i> series, and shades in some very welcome complexity and heartbreak for Luke, one of the unfortunate antagonists in the battle between the Gods and the Titans. His relationship with Thalia and Annabeth takes shape before our eyes, and it's a treat as well to witness his meeting with the miserably accursed Halcyon Green and watch how this both reinforces and underpins Luke's motives in the story he has yet to live. With Halcyon (and even Luke), Riordan somehow manages to again pull off that magic trick he performs so well of giving even minor characters surprising amounts of emotional depth and resonance, despite the fact that they spend most of their limited appearances as snarky, post-modern approximations of their mythological counterparts.<br /><br />The other two stories - <i>Percy Jackson And The Staff Of Hermes</i> and <i>Leo Valdez And The Quest For Buford</i> - are more light-hearted entries in Riordan's canon, but also hit just the right spot in reminding readers of everything that's at stake in the next book in the <i>Heroes Of Olympus</i> series. In the former tale, he allows us a peek at Percy and Annabeth's fledgling relationship before Percy is spirited away and dosed with amnesia. It's as sparky, banter-filled and irreverent as anything Riordan has previously cooked up for his protagonists, and reminds us even as we tag along on Percy and Annabeth's quest to track a thief into the sewers of Manhattan how much we've missed seeing these two together in the main series of books. Leo's adventure similarly gives us a breather from the doom and gloom that will likely be the lot of these characters in time to come; instead, we get to spend a little time with Leo, Piper and Jason as they try their best to set matters right when a couple of very important metal doo-wat-sits disappear from Bunker 9. <br /><br />Perhaps of greatest interest to anyone picking up a copy of <i>Diaries</i> would be the fact that Riordan's eldest son, Haley, has contributed a yarn of his own - <i>Son Of Magic</i> - to the fictional world his dad created for him as a bedtime story. How does young Haley acquit himself as a storyteller? On the strength of this particular tale, I'd say rather well. His prose is a little more stilted than his dad's, and apart from a couple of throwaway moments, lacks the silly humour the elder Riordan so effortlessly weaves into action sequences. But Haley's story deepens and grows as it goes along, so that we - alongside the arrogant Professor Claymore and the wonderfully-named Alabaster Torrington - eventually get swept up in his narrative. It's a worthy entry in Percy's world, and one that answers quite a lot of questions about how magic operates in the universe... questions Haley's father hadn't even thought to answer!<br /><br />All in all, <i>Diaries</i> does exactly what it sets out to do: provide a little more background to the characters through stories that don't quite fit into the larger narrative that Riordan is currently spinning across all his novels, while still getting his readers thoroughly excited for <i>Athena</i>. Is it October 2nd yet?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3561549549176851927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360797193" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360797193" />
    <a title="Cathy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526945-cathy"><img alt="Cathy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391558556p2/1526945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360797193?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy " href="/user/show/1526945-cathy">Cathy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=juvenile">juvenile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526945-cathy?shelf=urban">urban</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360797193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17689027425894566100">These extra little books that Riordan puts out about his two mythology series are never terribly substantial, but they're not really meant to be. From what I remember of the others, this was most satisfying to me as an adult reader because it had 4 quite solid stories and less of the games, pictures, and extras that might appeal to juvenile readers, but probably aren't of much interest even to young adult readers, much less adults. It's hard to balance these things because the books are popular </span>
  <span id="freeText17689027425894566100" style="display:none">These extra little books that Riordan puts out about his two mythology series are never terribly substantial, but they're not really meant to be. From what I remember of the others, this was most satisfying to me as an adult reader because it had 4 quite solid stories and less of the games, pictures, and extras that might appeal to juvenile readers, but probably aren't of much interest even to young adult readers, much less adults. It's hard to balance these things because the books are popular with so many audiences, but I know as an adult reader that the books really aren't aimed at me so I try not to judge too harshly.<br /><br />The first story was about Luke's history with Thalia. It portrayed him as a brave and lonely young boy and was quite poignant. It also showed one of the experiences that he had that put him on his dangerous path, as he learned that that the gods could be very cruel to the demigods and that the kids had to defend themselves because, as usual, their godly parent sure as Olympus weren't going to intervene. "I will learn from your mistakes. If the gods ever treat me that badly, I will fight back." I couldn't help but feel for the kid, knowing where he started, and so many of the things he went through. <br /><br />The second story was cute, classic Percy/Riordan with humor and adventure. It was mostly just a cute bridge for fans between the first and second series. I'm not sure I got anything new out of it, but it was a cute story. <br /><br />Pretty much the same is true of the third story. I think Riordan is walking the line of trying to write satisfying stories for fans but making sure that people who don't read this book don't miss out on anything substantial, so the stories are fun but don't add anything big to the plot of the series. This one is about Piper, Leo and Jason at the camp. I liked the use of mythology. It did move the story along a bit, talking about Leo building the Argo II, but mostly it just helped me get even more excited to read the next book. <br /><br />As for the story, it was very cool that it was written by Haley Riordan, especially given his role as the inspiration for all of the Percy stories. And when you consider his personal journey to overcome dyslexia and ADHD, and the fact that he's only 16 himself, it's pretty remarkable. It was a surprisingly mature story for a 16 year-old, I'd never have guess that a kid wrote it. It definitely felt a bit like fan-fiction to me just because it was clearly a different style than the rest of the book; he got the sense of adventure and danger pretty well, but it lacked the humor and lightness of the senior Riordan's writing. Which is fine, I don't think he was trying to copy his dad, it just did stand out as different. And it was kind of an odd choice for this series to make the main character an adult, and an older adult, that was just kind of weird to me. If I didn't really connect to the guy and I'm in my 40s, then how did the kids who are the target audience of the book feel about him? I did really like the choice of using a kid from the Kronos side of the war, that was interesting. And the Lamia was a really scary monster. Overall it was a good story.<br /><br />It really should be a 3.5 star book, but since it was more substantial than the other little filler books that Riordan has put out, I'll round it up to 4. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17689027425894566100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_391719000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/391719000" />
    <a title="Sarah Schanze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3451643-sarah-schanze"><img alt="Sarah Schanze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524436787p2/3451643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/391719000?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Schanze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Schanze" href="/user/show/3451643-sarah-schanze">Sarah Schanze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3451643-sarah-schanze?shelf=kids-section">kids-section</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer391719000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6882504474342744729">This book is basically divided into two parts: what Rick Riordan wrote and what his son Haley wrote.<br/><br/>Everything Rick wrote was, as usual, charming and funny and exciting and cute. He's one of my favorite writers because he knows how to balance the light and the dark, and it never gets <i>too</i> dark, even in life or death situations. His books are perfect "escape" books. They're fluffy, and <i>I love that</i>. I know I'm going to enjoy myself no matter which world or character he's writing.<br/><br/>I would have given </span>
  <span id="freeText6882504474342744729" style="display:none">This book is basically divided into two parts: what Rick Riordan wrote and what his son Haley wrote.<br /><br />Everything Rick wrote was, as usual, charming and funny and exciting and cute. He's one of my favorite writers because he knows how to balance the light and the dark, and it never gets <i>too</i> dark, even in life or death situations. His books are perfect "escape" books. They're fluffy, and <i>I love that</i>. I know I'm going to enjoy myself no matter which world or character he's writing.<br /><br />I would have given this book four stars, but the very last story, "Son of Magic", knocked one off. Haley is a great writer for 16, and his stuff is years ahead what I was writing when I was 16, but the story just didn't fit. The main protagonist wasn't a demigod, and wasn't very likeable even at the end of the story. He uses a gun to try and kill a monster, and for some reason the appearance of guns, working guns that shoot bullets, in this world was disconcerting to me. It's almost too "real", and it knocks the tone down from exciting to a bit dark. Especially when the main protagonist kicks a monster's jaw so hard it flies off her face (as dust, but still). I also didn't like how Hecate was portrayed as a white-robed Virgin Mary wannabe praying at a church altar. What's that supposed to tell us? It's left unanswered but I definitely don't like the idea of these mythical Greek gods worshiping the Christian god. That sends a bad message.<br /><br />Haley did not write <i>badly</i>. He knew how to pace and describe things, and it didn't feel clunky and choppy. It just didn't fit the tone of the world his father has established. He might be trying to inject some maturity into it, but I don't want that at all. I'll stick with Rick.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6882504474342744729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_799093495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/799093495" />
    <a title="Mender" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7349719-mender"><img alt="Mender" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592480715p2/7349719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/799093495?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mender" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mender" href="/user/show/7349719-mender">Mender</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer799093495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14366768816932429072">So this happened to be on my library shelf, and it's the sort of thing you could read in a few hours. Except that I can't just read short stories in a sitting, their changing storylines annoy me and make me put it down and the whole thing take longer. Anyway, that's a glitch with my system rather than the book. This is a lot of in between stories, where not a great deal happens but it's all light fluffy fun. Only without the sense of it all going anywhere.<br/><br/>The standout is Rick's son's contributio</span>
  <span id="freeText14366768816932429072" style="display:none">So this happened to be on my library shelf, and it's the sort of thing you could read in a few hours. Except that I can't just read short stories in a sitting, their changing storylines annoy me and make me put it down and the whole thing take longer. Anyway, that's a glitch with my system rather than the book. This is a lot of in between stories, where not a great deal happens but it's all light fluffy fun. Only without the sense of it all going anywhere.<br /><br />The standout is Rick's son's contribution in the last story, which is a remarkably well written story for any age. It's empathic towards the demigods who fought with Kronos during the wars in the first Percy Jackson series. Thought provoking, the monsters here are the more dangerous kind that come up in the real myths. It's all much more gritty and full of consequences and quite a bit smarter than the average Rick Riordan book. Which means that I'm happy to read the one story, but a whole book worth of it just wouldn't hold up in the Percy Jackson universe. It's too slapstick a place for this sort of introspection.<br /><br />But Haley Riordan has caught my eye for his insight and control of language, so I'll pick up his debut when and if it comes out/I find it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14366768816932429072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2430231024842641884"> Once again Rick Riordan failed to disappoint me with another one of his amazing books. My favorite part of this book is the Luke's diary because he explains his beginning and how he became the villain he was. I also liked that the book had a quiz to see if you could guess the god's roman form. I liked that because it actually made think about what you read about the gods. Unfortunately I didn't think this book was better than the demigod files because WHO NEEDS THE ROMANS?!(No offense to Jason </span>

My favorite part of this book is the Luke's diary because he explains his beginning and how he became the villain he was. I also liked that the book had a quiz to see if you could guess the god's roman form. I liked that because it actually made think about what you read about the gods. Unfortunately I didn't think this book was better than the demigod files because WHO NEEDS THE ROMANS?!(No offense to Jason fans)The story about Jason, Leo, and Piper was good, its just that they can't beat the original characters.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tjylUvqu/HTQto9xrZGP/y7jm5TWDZ7lR5+cGxsazReMGsyAQfA1HHedOxBaZIUg+Lx8XBiAEIIc4dqq1lk/jQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('83FfHjRdBSZUJ6RA02MtGjLJcDOSyUmltg3QEPkJL7fJVzbMjwPMTvMMECEklifF5JaX+1xEx8Ltc5ahNErdLQ==')})
  }
